   <h1 class="firstHeading" id="firstHeading" lang="en">
    Curaçao
   </h1>

      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       Not to be confused with
       <a class="mw-redirect mw-disambig" href="/wiki/Curacoa_(disambiguation)" title="Curacoa (disambiguation)">
        Curacoa
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Curassow" title="Curassow">
        Curassow
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Carriacou" title="Carriacou">
        Carriacou
       </a>
       , or
       <a href="/wiki/Curu%C3%A7%C3%A1_River_(Javari_River)" title="Curuçá River (Javari River)">
        Curuçá River (Javari River)
       </a>
       .
      </div>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       This article is about the island country. For the former colony/territory comprising Curaçao and five other islands, see
       <a href="/wiki/Cura%C3%A7ao_and_Dependencies" title="Curaçao and Dependencies">
        Curaçao and Dependencies
       </a>
       . For the liqueur, see
       <a href="/wiki/Cura%C3%A7ao_(liqueur)" title="Curaçao (liqueur)">
        Curaçao (liqueur)
       </a>
       .
      </div>

        </th>

      <p>
       <b>
        Curaçao
       </b>
       (
       <span class="nowrap">
        <span class="IPA nopopups noexcerpt">
         <a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/English" title="Help:IPA/English">
          /
          <span style="border-bottom:1px dotted">
           <span title="/ˈ/: primary stress follows">
            ˈ
           </span>
           <span title="'k' in 'kind'">
            k
           </span>
           <span title="/ʊr/: 'our' in 'courier'">
            ʊr
           </span>
           <span title="/ə/: 'a' in 'about'">
            ə
           </span>
           <span title="'s' in 'sigh'">
            s
           </span>
           <span title="/aʊ/: 'ou' in 'mouth'">
            aʊ
           </span>
          </span>
          /
         </a>
        </span>
       </span>
       <a href="/wiki/Help:Pronunciation_respelling_key" title="Help:Pronunciation respelling key">
        <i title="English pronunciation respelling">
         <span style="font-size:90%">
          KUR
         </span>
         -ə-sow
        </i>
       </a>
       or
       <span class="nowrap">
        <span class="IPA nopopups noexcerpt">
         <a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/English" title="Help:IPA/English">
          /
          <span style="border-bottom:1px dotted">
           <span title="/ˈ/: primary stress follows">
            ˈ
           </span>
           <span title="'k' in 'kind'">
            k
           </span>
           <span title="/jʊər/: 'ure' in 'cure'">
            jʊər
           </span>
           <span title="/ə/: 'a' in 'about'">
            ə
           </span>
           <span title="'s' in 'sigh'">
            s
           </span>
           <span title="/aʊ/: 'ou' in 'mouth'">
            aʊ
           </span>
          </span>
          /
         </a>
        </span>
       </span>
       <a href="/wiki/Help:Pronunciation_respelling_key" title="Help:Pronunciation respelling key">
        <i title="English pronunciation respelling">
         <span style="font-size:90%">
          KEWR
         </span>
         -ə-sow
        </i>
       </a>
       ;
       <a href="/wiki/Dutch_language" title="Dutch language">
        Dutch
       </a>
       :
       <i>
        <span lang="nl" xml:lang="nl">
         Curaçao
        </span>
       </i>
       ,
       <small>
        pronounced
       </small>
       <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
        <a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/Dutch" title="Help:IPA/Dutch">
         [kyːraːˈsʌu̯]
        </a>
       </span>
       ;
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-6">
        <a href="#cite_note-6">
         [6]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Papiamento_language" title="Papiamento language">
        Papiamento
       </a>
       :
       <i>
        <span lang="pap" xml:lang="pap">
         Kòrsou
        </span>
       </i>
       ) is a
       <a href="/wiki/Lesser_Antilles" title="Lesser Antilles">
        Lesser Antilles
       </a>
       <a href="/wiki/Island" title="Island">
        island
       </a>
       in the southern
       <a href="/wiki/Caribbean_Sea" title="Caribbean Sea">
        Caribbean Sea
       </a>
       and the
       <a href="/wiki/Dutch_Caribbean" title="Dutch Caribbean">
        Dutch Caribbean
       </a>
       region, about 65 km (40 mi) north of the
       <a href="/wiki/Venezuela" title="Venezuela">
        Venezuelan
       </a>
       coast. It is a constituent country (
       <a href="/wiki/Dutch_language" title="Dutch language">
        Dutch
       </a>
       :
       <i>
        <span lang="nl" xml:lang="nl">
         land
        </span>
       </i>
       ) of the
       <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_the_Netherlands" title="Kingdom of the Netherlands">
        Kingdom of the Netherlands
       </a>
       .
      </p>
      <p>
       The country was formerly part of the
       <a href="/wiki/Cura%C3%A7ao_and_Dependencies" title="Curaçao and Dependencies">
        Curaçao and Dependencies
       </a>
       colony (1815–1954) and is now formally called the
       <b>
        Country of Curaçao
       </b>
       (Dutch:
       <i>
        <span lang="nl" xml:lang="nl">
         Land Curaçao
        </span>
       </i>
       ;
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-7">
        <a href="#cite_note-7">
         [7]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Papiamento:
       <i>
        <span lang="pap" xml:lang="pap">
         Pais Kòrsou
        </span>
       </i>
       );
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-8">
        <a href="#cite_note-8">
         [8]
        </a>
       </sup>
       it includes the main island of Curaçao and the uninhabited island of
       <a href="/wiki/Klein_Cura%C3%A7ao" title="Klein Curaçao">
        Klein Curaçao
       </a>
       ("Little Curaçao"). It has a
       <a href="/wiki/Population" title="Population">
        population
       </a>
       over 160,000 in an area of 444 km
       <sup>
        2
       </sup>
       (171
       <a href="/wiki/Square_mile" title="Square mile">
        sq mi
       </a>
       ), and its capital is
       <a href="/wiki/Willemstad" title="Willemstad">
        Willemstad
       </a>
       .
      </p>
      <p>
       Before the
       <a href="/wiki/Dissolution_of_the_Netherlands_Antilles" title="Dissolution of the Netherlands Antilles">
        dissolution of the Netherlands Antilles
       </a>
       on 10 October 2010, Curaçao was administered as the "Island Territory of Curaçao"
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-9">
        <a href="#cite_note-9">
         [9]
        </a>
       </sup>
       (Dutch:
       <i>
        <span lang="nl" xml:lang="nl">
         Eilandgebied Curaçao
        </span>
       </i>
       , Papiamento:
       <i>
        <span lang="pap" xml:lang="pap">
         Teritorio Insular di Kòrsou
        </span>
       </i>
       ), one of five
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/List_of_islands_of_the_Netherlands_Antilles" title="List of islands of the Netherlands Antilles">
        island territories
       </a>
       of the former Netherlands Antilles.
      </p>
      <p>
      </p>

          </span>

        </li>
       </ul>
      </div>
      <p>
      </p>
      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Etymology">
        Etymology
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Cura%C3%A7ao&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Etymology">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>
      <p>
       In the 16th and 17th centuries, sailors on long voyages would get scurvy from lack of vitamin C. According to some accounts, Portuguese sailors who were ill were left at the island now known as Curaçao. When their ship returned, they had recovered, likely cured from
       <a href="/wiki/Scurvy" title="Scurvy">
        scurvy
       </a>
       , probably after eating fruit with vitamin C. From then on the Portuguese referred to this as
       <i>
        Ilha da Curação
       </i>
       (Island of Healing). Another explanation is that it is derived from the Portuguese word for heart (coração), referring to the island as a centre in trade. An unstressed
       <i>
        o
       </i>
       in Continental Portuguese is usually pronounced [u], so the Portuguese word for heart, coração, is actually pronounced [kurɐsãw]. Spanish traders took the name over as Curaçao, which was followed by the Dutch.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-curacao-nature_10-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-curacao-nature-10">
         [10]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       Another explanation is that Curaçao was the name by which the indigenous peoples of the island identified themselves, their autonym. (Joubert and Van Buurt, 1994). Early Spanish accounts support this theory, as they refer to the indigenous peoples as
       <i>
        Indios Curaçaos,
       </i>
       or "healing Indians".
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-curacao-nature_10-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-curacao-nature-10">
         [10]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       From 1525, the island was featured on Spanish maps as
       <i>
        Curaçote, Curasaote,
       </i>
       and
       <i>
        Curasaore.
       </i>
       By the 17th century, it appeared on most maps in Portuguese as
       <i>
        Curaçao
       </i>
       or
       <i>
        Curazao.
       </i>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-curacao-nature_10-2">
        <a href="#cite_note-curacao-nature-10">
         [10]
        </a>
       </sup>
       On a map created by
       <a href="/wiki/Hieronymus_Cock" title="Hieronymus Cock">
        Hieronymus Cock
       </a>
       in 1562 in
       <a href="/wiki/Antwerp" title="Antwerp">
        Antwerp
       </a>
       , the island was referred to as
       <i>
        Qúracao.
       </i>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-11">
        <a href="#cite_note-11">
         [11]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="History">
        History
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Cura%C3%A7ao&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: History">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       Main article:
       <a href="/wiki/History_of_Cura%C3%A7ao" title="History of Curaçao">
        History of Curaçao
       </a>
      </div>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="First_inhabitants">
        First inhabitants
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Cura%C3%A7ao&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: First inhabitants">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:1562_Americae-Gutierrez_map_10hrs-inn_Sth-Florida-Cuba-Spagnola-Benezuela-to-Lesser-Antilles.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2330" data-file-width="2660" height="193" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1f/1562_Americae-Gutierrez_map_10hrs-inn_Sth-Florida-Cuba-Spagnola-Benezuela-to-Lesser-Antilles.jpg/220px-1562_Americae-Gutierrez_map_10hrs-inn_Sth-Florida-Cuba-Spagnola-Benezuela-to-Lesser-Antilles.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1f/1562_Americae-Gutierrez_map_10hrs-inn_Sth-Florida-Cuba-Spagnola-Benezuela-to-Lesser-Antilles.jpg/330px-1562_Americae-Gutierrez_map_10hrs-inn_Sth-Florida-Cuba-Spagnola-Benezuela-to-Lesser-Antilles.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1f/1562_Americae-Gutierrez_map_10hrs-inn_Sth-Florida-Cuba-Spagnola-Benezuela-to-Lesser-Antilles.jpg/440px-1562_Americae-Gutierrez_map_10hrs-inn_Sth-Florida-Cuba-Spagnola-Benezuela-to-Lesser-Antilles.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:1562_Americae-Gutierrez_map_10hrs-inn_Sth-Florida-Cuba-Spagnola-Benezuela-to-Lesser-Antilles.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         Map from 1562 with Curaçao indicated as Qúracao
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Cura%C3%A7ao1836.png">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1964" data-file-width="2366" height="183" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cf/Cura%C3%A7ao1836.png/220px-Cura%C3%A7ao1836.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cf/Cura%C3%A7ao1836.png/330px-Cura%C3%A7ao1836.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cf/Cura%C3%A7ao1836.png/440px-Cura%C3%A7ao1836.png 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Cura%C3%A7ao1836.png" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         Map of Curaçao in 1836
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       The original inhabitants of Curaçao were
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Arawak_people" title="Arawak people">
        Arawak people
       </a>
       . Their ancestors had migrated to the island from the mainland of South America, likely hundreds of years before Europeans arrived. They were believed to have migrated from the Amazon Basin.
      </p>
      <p>
       The first Europeans recorded as seeing the island were members of a Spanish expedition under the leadership of
       <a href="/wiki/Alonso_de_Ojeda" title="Alonso de Ojeda">
        Alonso de Ojeda
       </a>
       in 1499. The Spaniards enslaved most of the Arawak as their labour force. They sometimes forcibly relocated the survivors to other colonies where workers were needed. In 1634, after the Netherlands achieved independence from Spain, Dutch colonists started to occupy the island. European powers were trying to establish bases in the Caribbean.
      </p>
      <p>
       The
       <a href="/wiki/Dutch_West_India_Company" title="Dutch West India Company">
        Dutch West India Company
       </a>
       founded the capital of Willemstad on the banks of an inlet called the Schottegat. Curaçao had been ignored by colonists, because it lacked gold deposits. The
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Natural_harbour" title="Natural harbour">
        natural harbour
       </a>
       of Willemstad proved to be an ideal spot for trade. Commerce and shipping—and
       <a href="/wiki/Piracy_in_the_Caribbean" title="Piracy in the Caribbean">
        piracy
       </a>
       —became Curaçao's most important economic activities. In addition, in 1662, the Dutch West India Company made Curaçao a centre for the
       <a href="/wiki/Atlantic_slave_trade" title="Atlantic slave trade">
        Atlantic slave trade
       </a>
       , often bringing slaves here for sale elsewhere in the Caribbean and on the mainland of South America.
      </p>
      <p>
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sephardic_Jews" title="Sephardic Jews">
        Sephardic Jews
       </a>
       with ancestors from the Iberian Peninsula settled here with the Dutch and in then-
       <a href="/wiki/Dutch_Brazil" title="Dutch Brazil">
        Dutch Brazil
       </a>
       ; they have had a significant influence on the culture and economy of the island.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-history_12-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-history-12">
         [12]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       In the
       <a href="/wiki/Franco-Dutch_War" title="Franco-Dutch War">
        Franco-Dutch War
       </a>
       , Count
       <a href="/wiki/Jean_II_d%27Estr%C3%A9es" title="Jean II d'Estrées">
        Jean II d'Estrées
       </a>
       planned to attack Curaçao. His fleet — 12 men of war, three fireships, two transports, a hospital ship, and 12 privateers — met with disaster, losing seven men-of-war and two other ships when they struck reefs off the
       <a href="/wiki/Las_Aves_archipelago" title="Las Aves archipelago">
        Las Aves archipelago
       </a>
       . They had made a serious navigational error, hitting the reefs on 11 May 1678, a week after setting sail from
       <a href="/wiki/Saint_Kitts" title="Saint Kitts">
        Saint Kitts
       </a>
       . Curaçao marked the events by a day of thanksgiving, celebrated for decades into the 18th century, to commemorate the island's escape from being invaded by the French.
      </p>
      <p>
       Although a few
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Plantations" title="Plantations">
        plantations
       </a>
       were established on the island by the Dutch, the first profitable industry established on Curaçao was
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Salt_mines" title="Salt mines">
        salt mining
       </a>
       . The mineral was a lucrative export at the time and was a major factor for the island being part of international commerce.
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Emergence_of_Willemstad">
        Emergence of Willemstad
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Cura%C3%A7ao&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Emergence of Willemstad">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Cura%C3%A7ao,_Broad_Street.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1279" data-file-width="1745" height="161" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8e/Cura%C3%A7ao%2C_Broad_Street.jpg/220px-Cura%C3%A7ao%2C_Broad_Street.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8e/Cura%C3%A7ao%2C_Broad_Street.jpg/330px-Cura%C3%A7ao%2C_Broad_Street.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8e/Cura%C3%A7ao%2C_Broad_Street.jpg/440px-Cura%C3%A7ao%2C_Broad_Street.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Cura%C3%A7ao,_Broad_Street.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         Willemstad, 1885
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       Many Dutch colonists grew affluent from the slave trade, and the city built impressive colonial buildings. Curaçao architecture blends Dutch and Spanish colonial styles. The wide range of historic buildings in and around Willemstad has resulted in the capital being designated as a
       <a href="/wiki/UNESCO" title="UNESCO">
        UNESCO
       </a>
       <a href="/wiki/World_Heritage_Site" title="World Heritage Site">
        World Heritage Site
       </a>
       . Landhouses (former plantation estates) and West African style
       <i>
        kas di pal'i maishi
       </i>
       (former slave dwellings) are scattered all over the island. Some have been restored and can be visited.
      </p>
      <p>
       In 1795, a major
       <a href="/wiki/Cura%C3%A7ao_Slave_Revolt_of_1795" title="Curaçao Slave Revolt of 1795">
        slave revolt
       </a>
       took place under the leaders
       <a href="/wiki/Tula_(Cura%C3%A7ao)" title="Tula (Curaçao)">
        Tula Rigaud
       </a>
       , Louis Mercier, Bastian Karpata, and Pedro Wakao. Up to 4000 slaves on the northwest section of the island revolted. More than 1,000 slaves took part in extended gunfights. After a month, the slave owners suppressed the revolt.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-13">
        <a href="#cite_note-13">
         [13]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Luis_Bri%C3%B3n_2012_000.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2480" data-file-width="2272" height="240" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/be/Luis_Bri%C3%B3n_2012_000.jpg/220px-Luis_Bri%C3%B3n_2012_000.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/be/Luis_Bri%C3%B3n_2012_000.jpg/330px-Luis_Bri%C3%B3n_2012_000.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/be/Luis_Bri%C3%B3n_2012_000.jpg/440px-Luis_Bri%C3%B3n_2012_000.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Luis_Bri%C3%B3n_2012_000.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         <a href="/wiki/Luis_Bri%C3%B3n" title="Luis Brión">
          Luis Brión
         </a>
         , a Curaçao-born
         <a href="/wiki/Venezuela" title="Venezuela">
          Venezuelan
         </a>
         admiral
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       Curaçao's proximity to
       <a href="/wiki/South_America" title="South America">
        South America
       </a>
       resulted in interaction with cultures of the coastal areas. Architectural similarities can be seen between the 19th-century parts of Willemstad and the nearby Venezuelan city of
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Santa_Ana_de_Coro" title="Santa Ana de Coro">
        Coro
       </a>
       in
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Falc%C3%B3n_State" title="Falcón State">
        Falcón State
       </a>
       . The latter has also been designated a UNESCO World Heritage Site. In the 19th century, Curaçaoans such as
       <a href="/wiki/Manuel_Piar" title="Manuel Piar">
        Manuel Piar
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Luis_Bri%C3%B3n" title="Luis Brión">
        Luis Brión
       </a>
       were prominently engaged in the wars of independence of Venezuela and
       <a href="/wiki/Colombia" title="Colombia">
        Colombia
       </a>
       . Political refugees from the mainland (such as
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Simon_Bolivar" title="Simon Bolivar">
        Simon Bolivar
       </a>
       ) regrouped in Curaçao. Children from affluent Venezuelan families were educated on the island.
      </p>
      <p>
       During the 18th and 19th centuries, the island changed hands among the British, the French, and the Dutch several times. In the early 19th century, Portuguese and Lebanese migrated to Curaçao, attracted by the business opportunities. Stable Dutch rule returned in 1815 at the end of the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Napoleonic_wars" title="Napoleonic wars">
        Napoleonic wars
       </a>
       , when the island was incorporated into the colony of
       <a href="/wiki/Cura%C3%A7ao_and_Dependencies" title="Curaçao and Dependencies">
        Curaçao and Dependencies
       </a>
       .
      </p>
      <p>
       The Dutch abolished slavery in 1863, bringing a change in the economy with the shift to wage labour. Some inhabitants of Curaçao emigrated to other islands, such as
       <a href="/wiki/Cuba" title="Cuba">
        Cuba
       </a>
       , to work in
       <a href="/wiki/Sugar_plantations_in_the_Caribbean" title="Sugar plantations in the Caribbean">
        sugarcane plantations
       </a>
       . Other former slaves had nowhere to go and remained working for the plantation owner in the
       <a href="/wiki/Tenant_farmer" title="Tenant farmer">
        tenant farmer
       </a>
       system.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-14">
        <a href="#cite_note-14">
         [14]
        </a>
       </sup>
       This was an instituted order in which the former slave leased land from his former master. In exchange, the tenant promised to give up for rent most of his harvest to the former slave master. This system lasted until the beginning of the 20th century.
      </p>
      <p>
       Historically, Dutch was not widely spoken on the island outside of colonial administration; its use increased in the late 19th and early 20th centuries.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Putte_15-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-Putte-15">
         [15]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Students on Curaçao, Aruba, and Bonaire were taught predominantly in Spanish until the late 19th century. Also, efforts were made to introduce bilingual popular education in Dutch and Papiamentu in the late 19th century.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-16">
        <a href="#cite_note-16">
         [16]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       When oil was discovered in the
       <a href="/wiki/Maracaibo_Basin" title="Maracaibo Basin">
        Maracaibo Basin
       </a>
       town of Mene Grande in 1914, the fortunes of the island were dramatically altered. In the early years, both Shell and
       <a href="/wiki/Exxon" title="Exxon">
        Exxon
       </a>
       held drilling concessions in Venezuela, which ensured a constant supply of crude oil to the refineries in Aruba and Curaçao. Crude oil production in Venezuela was inexpensive. The integrated companies Shell and Exxon controlled the entire industry from pumping, transporting, and refining to marketing the end product. The refineries on Aruba and Curaçao operated in global markets and were profitable partly because of the margin between the production costs of crude oil and the revenues realized on products. This provided a safety net for losses incurred through inefficiency or excessive operating costs at the refineries.
      </p>
      <p>
       One of the best-known events that occurred in Curaçao during the 20th century is the
       <a href="/wiki/1969_Cura%C3%A7ao_uprising" title="1969 Curaçao uprising">
        1969 Curaçao uprising
       </a>
       . The riots damaged Willemstad and resulted in the resignation of the Prime Minister as well as a social prestige for the local language Papiamento.
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Recent_timeline">
        Recent timeline
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Cura%C3%A7ao&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Recent timeline">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Willemstad_harbor.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1728" data-file-width="2304" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b0/Willemstad_harbor.jpg/220px-Willemstad_harbor.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b0/Willemstad_harbor.jpg/330px-Willemstad_harbor.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b0/Willemstad_harbor.jpg/440px-Willemstad_harbor.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Willemstad_harbor.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         Dutch architecture along
         <a href="/wiki/Willemstad" title="Willemstad">
          Willemstad
         </a>
         's harbour
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       Curaçao experienced an economic downturn in the early 1980s. Shell's refinery on Curaçao operated with significant losses from 1975 to 1979, and again from 1982 to 1985. Persistent losses, global
       <a href="/wiki/Overproduction" title="Overproduction">
        overproduction
       </a>
       , tougher competition, and low market expectations threatened the future of the Shell refinery in Curaçao. In 1985, after a presence of 70 years, Royal Dutch Shell decided to end its activities on Curaçao. Shell's announcement came at a crucial moment; the fragile economy of Curaçao had been stagnating for some time. Several revenue-generating endeavours suffered even more during this period: tourism from Venezuela collapsed after the devaluation of the bolivar, the transport industry deteriorated with deleterious effects on the profits of the Antillean Airline Company, and the Curaçao Dry Dock Company experienced major setbacks. The offshore industry (financial services) also experienced a downturn because of new tax laws in the United States.
      </p>
      <p>
       In the mid-1980s, Shell sold the refinery for the symbolic amount of one
       <a href="/wiki/Netherlands_Antillean_guilder" title="Netherlands Antillean guilder">
        Antillean guilder
       </a>
       to a local government consortium. The aging refinery has been the subject of lawsuits in recent years, which charge that its emissions, including
       <a href="/wiki/Sulfur_dioxide" title="Sulfur dioxide">
        sulfur dioxide
       </a>
       and
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Atmospheric_particulate_matter" title="Atmospheric particulate matter">
        particulate matter
       </a>
       , far exceed safety standards.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-17">
        <a href="#cite_note-17">
         [17]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The government consortium currently leases the refinery to the Venezuelan state oil company
       <a href="/wiki/PDVSA" title="PDVSA">
        PDVSA
       </a>
       .
      </p>
      <p>
       Due to an economic slump in the late 1990s and early 2000s, emigration to the Netherlands has been high.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-18">
        <a href="#cite_note-18">
         [18]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       On 1 July 2007, the island of Curaçao was due to become a country within the Kingdom of the Netherlands. On 28 November 2006, this was delayed when the island council rejected a clarification memorandum on the process. A new island council ratified this agreement on 9 July 2007.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-approved_19-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-approved-19">
         [19]
        </a>
       </sup>
       On 15 December 2008, Curaçao was scheduled to become a separate country within the Kingdom of the Netherlands (as Aruba and the Netherlands Antilles were). A non-binding referendum on this plan took place in Curaçao on 15 May 2009, in which 52 percent of the voters supported these plans.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-20">
        <a href="#cite_note-20">
         [20]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h4>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Since_the_dissolution_of_the_Netherlands_Antilles">
        Since the dissolution of the Netherlands Antilles
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Cura%C3%A7ao&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Since the dissolution of the Netherlands Antilles">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h4>
      <p>
       The
       <a href="/wiki/Dissolution_of_the_Netherlands_Antilles" title="Dissolution of the Netherlands Antilles">
        dissolution of the Netherlands Antilles
       </a>
       came into effect on 10 October 2010.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-21">
        <a href="#cite_note-21">
         [21]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-22">
        <a href="#cite_note-22">
         [22]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Curaçao became a country within the Kingdom of the Netherlands, with the Kingdom retaining responsibility for defence and foreign policy. The kingdom was also to oversee the island's finances under a debt-relief arrangement agreed between the two.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-23">
        <a href="#cite_note-23">
         [23]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Curaçao's first
       <a href="/wiki/Prime_Minister_of_Cura%C3%A7ao" title="Prime Minister of Curaçao">
        prime minister
       </a>
       was
       <a href="/wiki/Gerrit_Schotte" title="Gerrit Schotte">
        Gerrit Schotte
       </a>
       . He was succeeded in 2012 by
       <a href="/wiki/Stanley_Betrian" title="Stanley Betrian">
        Stanley Betrian
       </a>
       ,
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Ad_interim" title="Ad interim">
         ad interim
        </a>
       </i>
       . After elections in 2012
       <a href="/wiki/Daniel_Hodge" title="Daniel Hodge">
        Daniel Hodge
       </a>
       became the third prime minister, on 31 December 2012.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Hodge_24-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-Hodge-24">
         [24]
        </a>
       </sup>
       He led a
       <a href="/wiki/Demissionary_cabinet" title="Demissionary cabinet">
        demissionary cabinet
       </a>
       until 7 June 2013, when a new cabinet under the leadership of
       <a href="/wiki/Ivar_Asjes" title="Ivar Asjes">
        Ivar Asjes
       </a>
       was sworn in.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Asjes_25-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-Asjes-25">
         [25]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       Although Curaçao is autonomous, the Netherlands has interfered when necessary to ensure that parliamentary elections were held and to assist in finalizing an accurate budget. In July 2017, Prime Minister
       <a href="/wiki/Eugene_Rhuggenaath" title="Eugene Rhuggenaath">
        Eugene Rhuggenaath
       </a>
       stated that he wants the island to take full responsibility, but asked for more cooperation and assistance from the Netherlands with suggestions for more innovative approaches to help Curaçao succeed, increasing the standard of living.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-26">
        <a href="#cite_note-26">
         [26]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-27">
        <a href="#cite_note-27">
         [27]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The Dutch government reminded Curaçao that it has provided assistance with Oil Refinery negotiations with the Chinese "on numerous occasions".
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-28">
        <a href="#cite_note-28">
         [28]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Geography">
        Geography
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Cura%C3%A7ao&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Geography">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>
      <table class="plainlinks metadata ambox mbox-small-left ambox-content" role="presentation">

        </a>

          </a>

         Aerial view of Curacao
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">

         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="353" data-file-width="330" height="235" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a5/Curacao-CIA_WFB_Map.png/220px-Curacao-CIA_WFB_Map.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/a/a5/Curacao-CIA_WFB_Map.png 1.5x" width="220"/>
