      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Cura%C3%A7ao_-_Encyclopaedie_van_Nederlandsch_West-Indi%C3%AB-Antilles_part_2,_left.gif">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2868" data-file-width="3058" height="206" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/99/Cura%C3%A7ao_-_Encyclopaedie_van_Nederlandsch_West-Indi%C3%AB-Antilles_part_2%2C_left.gif/220px-Cura%C3%A7ao_-_Encyclopaedie_van_Nederlandsch_West-Indi%C3%AB-Antilles_part_2%2C_left.gif" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/99/Cura%C3%A7ao_-_Encyclopaedie_van_Nederlandsch_West-Indi%C3%AB-Antilles_part_2%2C_left.gif/330px-Cura%C3%A7ao_-_Encyclopaedie_van_Nederlandsch_West-Indi%C3%AB-Antilles_part_2%2C_left.gif 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/99/Cura%C3%A7ao_-_Encyclopaedie_van_Nederlandsch_West-Indi%C3%AB-Antilles_part_2%2C_left.gif/440px-Cura%C3%A7ao_-_Encyclopaedie_van_Nederlandsch_West-Indi%C3%AB-Antilles_part_2%2C_left.gif 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Cura%C3%A7ao_-_Encyclopaedie_van_Nederlandsch_West-Indi%C3%AB-Antilles_part_2,_left.gif" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         A detailed map of Curaçao from the
         <i>
          Encyclopaedie van Nederlandsch West-Indië 1914–1917
         </i>
         .
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       Curaçao, as well as the rest of the
       <a href="/wiki/ABC_islands_(Lesser_Antilles)" title="ABC islands (Lesser Antilles)">
        ABC islands
       </a>
       and also
       <a href="/wiki/Trinidad_and_Tobago" title="Trinidad and Tobago">
        Trinidad and Tobago
       </a>
       , lies on the continental shelf of South America, and is thus geologically considered to lie entirely in South America.
       <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">
        [
        <i>
         <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">
          <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (June 2014)">
           citation needed
          </span>
         </a>
        </i>
        ]
       </sup>
       Curaçao's highest point is the Sint Christoffelberg 372 m (1,220 ft)
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-29">
        <a href="#cite_note-29">
         [29]
        </a>
       </sup>
       . The coastlines bays, inlets and hot springs offer an on-site source of natural mineral, thermal, or seawater used in hydrotherapy and mesotherapy, making this island one of many
       <a href="/wiki/Balneotherapy" title="Balneotherapy">
        balneoclimateric
       </a>
       areas in the region.
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Flora">
        Flora
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Cura%C3%A7ao&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Flora">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <p>
       The flora of Curaçao differs from the typical tropical island vegetation.
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Xeric" title="Xeric">
        Xeric
       </a>
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Scrubland" title="Scrubland">
        scrublands
       </a>
       are common, with various forms of
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Cacti" title="Cacti">
        cacti
       </a>
       , thorny shrubs,
       <a href="/wiki/Evergreen" title="Evergreen">
        evergreen
       </a>
       , and the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Watapana" title="Watapana">
        watapana
       </a>
       tree, called
       <i>
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Divi-divi" title="Divi-divi">
         divi-divi
        </a>
       </i>
       on Aruba, characteristic for the ABC islands and the national symbol of Aruba.
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Fauna">
        Fauna
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Cura%C3%A7ao&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Fauna">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       Further information:
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Rodents_of_the_Caribbean#Curaçao" title="Rodents of the Caribbean">
        Rodents of the Caribbean § Curaçao
       </a>
      </div>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Climate">
        Climate
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Cura%C3%A7ao&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Climate">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <p>
       Curaçao has a
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Tropical_savannah_climate" title="Tropical savannah climate">
        tropical savannah climate
       </a>
       (
       <a href="/wiki/K%C3%B6ppen_climate_classification" title="Köppen climate classification">
        Köppen climate classification
       </a>
       <i>
        As
       </i>
       ) with a
       <a href="/wiki/Dry_season" title="Dry season">
        dry season
       </a>
       from January to September and a
       <a href="/wiki/Wet_season" title="Wet season">
        wet season
       </a>
       from October to December.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-meteoan_30-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-meteoan-30">
         [30]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The temperatures are relatively constant with small differences throughout the year. The
       <a href="/wiki/Trade_winds" title="Trade winds">
        trade winds
       </a>
       bring cooling during the day and the same trade winds bring warming during the night. The coolest month is January with an average temperature of 26.5 °C (80 °F) and the warmest month is September with an average temperature of 28.9 °C (84 °F). The year's average maximum temperature is 31.2 °C (88 °F). The year's average minimum temperature is 25.3 °C (78 °F).
      </p>
      <p>
       Curaçao lies outside the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hurricane_belt" title="Hurricane belt">
        hurricane belt
       </a>
       , but is still occasionally affected by hurricanes, as for example
       <a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Hazel" title="Hurricane Hazel">
        Hazel
       </a>
       in 1954,
       <a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Anna_(1961)" title="Hurricane Anna (1961)">
        Anna
       </a>
       in 1961,
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hurricane_Felix_(2007)" title="Hurricane Felix (2007)">
        Felix
       </a>
       in 2007, and
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hurricane_Omar_(2008)" title="Hurricane Omar (2008)">
        Omar
       </a>
       in 2008. A
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Landfall_(meteorology)" title="Landfall (meteorology)">
        landfall
       </a>
       of a
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hurricane" title="Hurricane">
        hurricane
       </a>
       in Curaçao has not occurred since the
       <a href="/wiki/United_States" title="United States">
        United States
       </a>
       <a href="/wiki/National_Hurricane_Center" title="National Hurricane Center">
        National Hurricane Center
       </a>
       started tracking hurricanes. Curaçao has, however, been directly affected by pre-hurricane tropical storms several times; the latest which to do so were
       <a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Tomas" title="Hurricane Tomas">
        Tomas
       </a>
       in 2010,
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hurricane_Cesar-Douglas" title="Hurricane Cesar-Douglas">
        Cesar
       </a>
       in 1996,
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hurricane_Joan-Miriam" title="Hurricane Joan-Miriam">
        Joan-Miriam
       </a>
       in 1988,
       <a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Cora" title="Hurricane Cora">
        Cora
       </a>
       and
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hurricane_Greta-Olivia" title="Hurricane Greta-Olivia">
        Greta
       </a>
       in 1978,
       <a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Edith_(1971)" title="Hurricane Edith (1971)">
        Edith
       </a>
       and
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hurricane_Irene_(1971)" title="Hurricane Irene (1971)">
        Irene
       </a>
       in 1971, and
       <a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Francelia" title="Hurricane Francelia">
        Francelia
       </a>
       in 1969. Tomas brushed Curaçao as a tropical storm, dropping as much as 265 mm (10.4 in) of precipitation on the territory, nearly half of the annual precipitation in one day.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-31">
        <a href="#cite_note-31">
         [31]
        </a>
       </sup>
       This made Tomas one of the wettest events in the island's history,
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-32">
        <a href="#cite_note-32">
         [32]
        </a>
       </sup>
       as well as one of the most devastating; its flooding killed two people and caused over NAƒ60 million (US$28 million) in damage.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-33">
        <a href="#cite_note-33">
         [33]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-34">
        <a href="#cite_note-34">
         [34]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       <a class="external text" href="http://www.meteo.cw" rel="nofollow">
        Meteo
       </a>
       , the Curaçao Weather Department, provides up to date information about weather conditions, via its website and
       <a class="external text" href="http://appstore.com/CuracaoWeather" rel="nofollow">
        mobile apps for iOS
       </a>
       and
       <a class="external text" href="https://play.google.com/store/apps/details?id=com.dwarfland.weather" rel="nofollow">
        Android
       </a>
       .
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Geology">
        Geology
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Cura%C3%A7ao&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Geology">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <p>
       The northern sea floor drops steeply within 60 m (200 ft) of the shore. This drop-off is known as the "blue edge".
      </p>
      <p>
       On Curaçao, four major geological formations can be found: The lava formation, the Knip formation, the Mid-Curaçao formation and Limestone formations.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-35">
        <a href="#cite_note-35">
         [35]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Forts">
        Forts
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Cura%C3%A7ao&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Forts">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <p>
       When the Dutch arrived in 1634, they built forts at key points around the island to protect themselves from foreign powers, privateers, and pirates. Six of the best-preserved forts can still be seen today:
      </p>
      <ul>
       <li>
        <a href="/wiki/Fort_Amsterdam_(Cura%C3%A7ao)" title="Fort Amsterdam (Curaçao)">
         Fort Amsterdam
        </a>
        (1635)
       </li>
       <li>
        Fort Beekenburg (1703)
       </li>
       <li>
        Fort Nassau (1797)
       </li>
       <li>
        Waterfort (1826)
       </li>
       <li>
        Riffort (1828)
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-36">
         <a href="#cite_note-36">
          [36]
         </a>
        </sup>
       </li>
       <li>
        Piscadera Bay Fort (built between 1701–1704)
       </li>
      </ul>
      <p>
       In 1957, the Hotel Van der Valk Plaza Curaçao was built on top of the Waterfort.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-37">
        <a href="#cite_note-37">
         [37]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       The Riffort contains restaurants and shops. It is located on the opposite side of the Waterfort across the entrance to the harbour. In 2009, the Renaissance Curaçao Resort and Casino opened next to the Riffort.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-38">
        <a href="#cite_note-38">
         [38]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-39">
        <a href="#cite_note-39">
         [39]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Government">
        Government
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Cura%C3%A7ao&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Government">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       Main article:
       <a href="/wiki/Government_of_Cura%C3%A7ao" title="Government of Curaçao">
        Government of Curaçao
       </a>
      </div>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:EU_OCT_and_OMR_map_en.png">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1358" data-file-width="2206" height="135" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/72/EU_OCT_and_OMR_map_en.png/220px-EU_OCT_and_OMR_map_en.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/72/EU_OCT_and_OMR_map_en.png/330px-EU_OCT_and_OMR_map_en.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/72/EU_OCT_and_OMR_map_en.png/440px-EU_OCT_and_OMR_map_en.png 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:EU_OCT_and_OMR_map_en.png" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         Map of the European Union in the world with overseas countries and territories and outermost regions
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       The government of Curaçao takes place in a framework of a
       <a href="/wiki/Parliamentary_system" title="Parliamentary system">
        parliamentary
       </a>
       <a href="/wiki/Representative_democracy" title="Representative democracy">
        representative democratic
       </a>
       <a href="/wiki/Country" title="Country">
        country
       </a>
       . The
       <a href="/wiki/Prime_Minister_of_Cura%C3%A7ao" title="Prime Minister of Curaçao">
        Prime Minister
       </a>
       is the
       <a href="/wiki/Head_of_government" title="Head of government">
        head of government
       </a>
       .
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Executive_power" title="Executive power">
        Executive power
       </a>
       is exercised by the government.
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Legislative_power" title="Legislative power">
        Legislative power
       </a>
       is vested in both the
       <a href="/wiki/Government" title="Government">
        government
       </a>
       and parliament.
      </p>
      <p>
       The
       <a href="/wiki/Judiciary" title="Judiciary">
        judiciary
       </a>
       is independent of the executive and the legislature. Convicted felons are held at the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sentro_di_Detenshon_i_Korekshon_K%C3%B2rsou" title="Sentro di Detenshon i Korekshon Kòrsou">
        Curaçao Centre for Detention and Correction
       </a>
       prison.
       <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">
        [
        <i>
         <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">
          <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (October 2013)">
           citation needed
          </span>
         </a>
        </i>
        ]
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       Curaçao has full autonomy on most matters, with the exceptions summed up in the
       <a href="/wiki/Charter_for_the_Kingdom_of_the_Netherlands" title="Charter for the Kingdom of the Netherlands">
        Charter for the Kingdom of the Netherlands
       </a>
       under the title "
       <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_the_Netherlands#Kingdom_affairs" title="Kingdom of the Netherlands">
        Kingdom affairs
       </a>
       ".
       <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">
        [
        <i>
         <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">
          <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (October 2013)">
           citation needed
          </span>
         </a>
        </i>
        ]
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Military">
        Military
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Cura%C3%A7ao&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Military">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>
      <p>
       Two
       <a href="/wiki/Royal_Netherlands_Navy" title="Royal Netherlands Navy">
        Dutch
       </a>
       naval bases, Parera and Suffisant, are located on the island of Curaçao. Officers of the
       <a href="/wiki/Military_of_Aruba" title="Military of Aruba">
        Arubaanse Militie
       </a>
       complete further training on Curaçao.
      </p>
      <p>
       On the west side of
       <a href="/wiki/Cura%C3%A7ao_International_Airport" title="Curaçao International Airport">
        Curaçao International Airport
       </a>
       are hangars for the two Bombardier Dash 8 Maritime Patrol Aircraft and two AgustaWestland AW139 helicopters of the Dutch Caribbean Coast Guard. This was until 2007 a naval airbase of the Royal Netherlands Navy, which operated the base for 55 years, with a wide variety of aircraft in the past years Fireflies, Avengers, Trackers, Neptunes, Fokker F-27's, P-3C Orions, Fokker F-60's and several helicopters. After the political decision to sell all Orions the airbase wasn't needed anymore.
      </p>
      <p>
       The west end of the airport is a
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/USAF" title="USAF">
        USAF
       </a>
       <a href="/wiki/Forward_Operating_Site" title="Forward Operating Site">
        Forward Operating Location
       </a>
       (FOL). The base hosts AWACS and transport aircraft. Until 1999 the USAF operated a small fleet of F-16 fighters from the FOB.
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Conscription">
        Conscription
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Cura%C3%A7ao&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Conscription">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <p>
       Suffisant Naval Base has facilities for conscription in the Caribbean, which has not been military conscription since 1997, but social conscription. This type of conscription offers underprivileged Antillean young people the chance of taking professional training.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-40">
        <a href="#cite_note-40">
         [40]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Economy">
        Economy
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Cura%C3%A7ao&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Economy">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       Main article:
       <a href="/wiki/Economy_of_Cura%C3%A7ao" title="Economy of Curaçao">
        Economy of Curaçao
       </a>
      </div>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Bohrinsel_Curacao_(34800864151).jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2242" data-file-width="3992" height="124" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f6/Bohrinsel_Curacao_%2834800864151%29.jpg/220px-Bohrinsel_Curacao_%2834800864151%29.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f6/Bohrinsel_Curacao_%2834800864151%29.jpg/330px-Bohrinsel_Curacao_%2834800864151%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f6/Bohrinsel_Curacao_%2834800864151%29.jpg/440px-Bohrinsel_Curacao_%2834800864151%29.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Bohrinsel_Curacao_(34800864151).jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         Offshore Oil platform in Curacao
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Historic_Area_of_Willemstad,_Inner_City_and_Harbour,_Cura%C3%A7ao-139159.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1200" data-file-width="1600" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c8/Historic_Area_of_Willemstad%2C_Inner_City_and_Harbour%2C_Cura%C3%A7ao-139159.jpg/220px-Historic_Area_of_Willemstad%2C_Inner_City_and_Harbour%2C_Cura%C3%A7ao-139159.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c8/Historic_Area_of_Willemstad%2C_Inner_City_and_Harbour%2C_Cura%C3%A7ao-139159.jpg/330px-Historic_Area_of_Willemstad%2C_Inner_City_and_Harbour%2C_Cura%C3%A7ao-139159.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c8/Historic_Area_of_Willemstad%2C_Inner_City_and_Harbour%2C_Cura%C3%A7ao-139159.jpg/440px-Historic_Area_of_Willemstad%2C_Inner_City_and_Harbour%2C_Cura%C3%A7ao-139159.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Historic_Area_of_Willemstad,_Inner_City_and_Harbour,_Cura%C3%A7ao-139159.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         Historic Area of Willemstad, declared
         <a href="/wiki/World_Heritage_Site" title="World Heritage Site">
          World Heritage Site
         </a>
         by
         <a href="/wiki/UNESCO" title="UNESCO">
          UNESCO
         </a>
         in 1997.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       Curaçao has an
       <a href="/wiki/Open_economy" title="Open economy">
        open economy
       </a>
       , with tourism, international trade, shipping services, oil refining,
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-41">
        <a href="#cite_note-41">
         [41]
        </a>
       </sup>
       storage (oil and bunkering) and international financial services being the most important sectors. The Venezuelan oil company
       <a href="/wiki/PDVSA" title="PDVSA">
        PDVSA
       </a>
       has a lease on the island's oil refinery expiring in 2019; the facility employs 1000 people, refining oil from Venezuela for export to the US and Asia.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-42">
        <a href="#cite_note-42">
         [42]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <a href="/wiki/Schlumberger" title="Schlumberger">
        Schlumberger
       </a>
       , the world's largest oil field services company is incorporated in Curaçao.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-43">
        <a href="#cite_note-43">
         [43]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The
       <a class="extiw" href="https://fr.wikipedia.org/wiki/Raffinerie_de_Isla" title="fr:Raffinerie de Isla">
        Isla oil refinery
       </a>
       is claimed to be responsible for Curaçao's position in the world's top five highest countries for CO2 emissions per capita.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-44">
        <a href="#cite_note-44">
         [44]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       Curaçao's has its own currency and its economy is well developed, supporting a high standard of living, ranking 46th in the world in terms of
       <a href="/wiki/List_of_countries_by_GDP_(PPP)_per_capita" title="List of countries by GDP (PPP) per capita">
        GDP (PPP) per capita
       </a>
       and 27th in the world in terms of
       <a href="/wiki/List_of_countries_by_GDP_(nominal)_per_capita" title="List of countries by GDP (nominal) per capita">
        nominal GDP per capita
       </a>
       . Curaçao possesses a
       <a href="/wiki/World_Bank_high-income_economy" title="World Bank high-income economy">
        high income economy
       </a>
       , as defined by the World Bank. Activities related to the port of Willemstad (like the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Free_Trade_Zone" title="Free Trade Zone">
        Free Trade Zone
       </a>
       ) make a significant contribution to the economy. To achieve the government's aim to make its economy more diverse, efforts are being made to attract more foreign investment. This policy, called the "Open Arms" policy, features a heavy focus on information technology companies.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-45">
        <a href="#cite_note-45">
         [45]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-46">
        <a href="#cite_note-46">
         [46]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-47">
        <a href="#cite_note-47">
         [47]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       Reduced foreign demand due to Venezuelan unrest has led to decreased exports along with increased public demands for services and goods which has resulted in economic stagnation since 2016. Expansion was recorded in the construction, financial intermediation, and utilities sectors while other aspects of the economy contracted.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-48">
        <a href="#cite_note-48">
         [48]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Tourism">
        Tourism
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Cura%C3%A7ao&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Tourism">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Curacao_Jan_Thiel_(34526956140).jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2242" data-file-width="3992" height="124" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2f/Curacao_Jan_Thiel_%2834526956140%29.jpg/220px-Curacao_Jan_Thiel_%2834526956140%29.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2f/Curacao_Jan_Thiel_%2834526956140%29.jpg/330px-Curacao_Jan_Thiel_%2834526956140%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2f/Curacao_Jan_Thiel_%2834526956140%29.jpg/440px-Curacao_Jan_Thiel_%2834526956140%29.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Curacao_Jan_Thiel_(34526956140).jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         Jan Thiel beach Curacao
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       While tourism plays a major role in Curaçao's economy, it is less reliant on tourism than other Caribbean countries. Most tourists originate from the Netherlands, Eastern United States, South America and other Caribbean Islands . It is a leader in the Caribbean in cruise tourism growth with 610,186 cruise passengers in 2013, a 41.4% increase over the prior year.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-CaribbeanInTourismGrowth_49-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-CaribbeanInTourismGrowth-49">
         [49]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hato_International_Airport" title="Hato International Airport">
        Hato International Airport
       </a>
       received 1,772,501 passengers in 2013 and recently announced capital investments totaling US$48 million aimed at transforming the airport into a regional hub by 2018. In 2017 the tourism sector was expected grow at 1% in terms of the total tourist stay over and by 15% in total cruise visitors versus 2016.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-50">
        <a href="#cite_note-50">
         [50]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       The island's
       <a href="/wiki/Continental_shelf" title="Continental shelf">
        insular shelf
       </a>
       has a sharp drop-off known as the "Blue Edge" which is often visited by
       <a href="/wiki/Scuba_diving" title="Scuba diving">
        Scuba diving
       </a>
       tourists.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-51">
        <a href="#cite_note-51">
         [51]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Coral reefs for
       <a href="/wiki/Snorkeling" title="Snorkeling">
        snorkeling
       </a>
       and scuba diving can be reached without a boat. The southern coast has calm waters as well as many small beaches, such as Jan Thiel and Cas Abou. The coastline of Curaçao features numerous bays and inlets which serve as popular mooring locations for boats.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-52">
        <a href="#cite_note-52">
         [52]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       In June 2017, the island was named the Top Cruise Destination in the Southern Caribbean by
       <a href="/wiki/Cruise_Critic" title="Cruise Critic">
        Cruise Critic
       </a>
       , a major online forum. The winners of the Destination Awards were selected based on comments from cruise passengers who rated the downtown area of Willemstad as "amazing" and the food and shopping as "excellent".
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-53">
        <a href="#cite_note-53">
         [53]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       Some of the coral reefs are affected by tourism.
       <a href="/wiki/Playa_Porto_Marie" title="Playa Porto Marie">
        Porto Marie Beach
       </a>
       is experimenting with artificial coral reefs in order to improve the reef's condition.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-54">
        <a href="#cite_note-54">
         [54]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Hundreds of artificial coral blocks that have been placed are now home to a large array of tropical fish.
      </p>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Curacao-Sea-Aquarium-2013.JPG">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2865" data-file-width="4573" height="138" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/13/Curacao-Sea-Aquarium-2013.JPG/220px-Curacao-Sea-Aquarium-2013.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/13/Curacao-Sea-Aquarium-2013.JPG/330px-Curacao-Sea-Aquarium-2013.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/13/Curacao-Sea-Aquarium-2013.JPG/440px-Curacao-Sea-Aquarium-2013.JPG 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Curacao-Sea-Aquarium-2013.JPG" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         The Curaçao Sea Aquarium and the Dolphin Academy share this islet on the west coast of Curaçao, with
         <a href="/wiki/Seaquarium_Beach" title="Seaquarium Beach">
          Seaquarium Beach
         </a>
         nearby.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Labour">
        Labour
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Cura%C3%A7ao&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Labour">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <p>
       In 2016, a Labor Force Survey (LFS) indicated that the unemployment rate was 13.3%. For residents aged 15–64, the employment rate was 70.4%.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-55">
        <a href="#cite_note-55">
         [55]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-56">
        <a href="#cite_note-56">
         [56]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Financial_services">
        Financial services
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Cura%C3%A7ao&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Financial services">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <p>
       Curaçao's history in
       <a href="/wiki/Financial_services" title="Financial services">
        financial services
       </a>
       dates back to
       <a href="/wiki/World_War_I" title="World War I">
        World War I
       </a>
       . Prior to this period, the financial arms of local merchant houses functioned as informal lenders to the community. However, at the turn of the century, Curaçao underwent industrialization, and a number of merchant houses established private
       <a href="/wiki/Commercial_bank" title="Commercial bank">
        commercial banks
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-57">
        <a href="#cite_note-57">
         [57]
        </a>
       </sup>
       As the economy grew, these banks began assuming additional functions eventually becoming full-fledged financial institutions.
      </p>
      <p>
       The
       <a href="/wiki/Dutch_Caribbean_Securities_Exchange" title="Dutch Caribbean Securities Exchange">
        Dutch Caribbean Securities Exchange
       </a>
       is located in the capital of Willemstad, as is the
       <a href="/wiki/Central_Bank_of_Cura%C3%A7ao_and_Sint_Maarten" title="Central Bank of Curaçao and Sint Maarten">
        Central Bank of Curaçao and Sint Maarten
       </a>
       ; the latter of which dates to 1828. It is the oldest
       <a href="/wiki/Central_bank" title="Central bank">
        central bank
       </a>
       in the Western Hemisphere.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-58">
        <a href="#cite_note-58">
         [58]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The island's legal system supports a variety of corporate structures and is a
       <a href="/wiki/Corporate_haven" title="Corporate haven">
        corporate haven
       </a>
       . Though Curaçao is considered a
       <a href="/wiki/Tax_haven" title="Tax haven">
        tax haven
       </a>
       , it adheres to the EU Code of Conduct against harmful tax practices. It holds a qualified intermediary status from the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/United_States_Internal_Revenue_Service" title="United States Internal Revenue Service">
        United States Internal Revenue Service
       </a>
       . It is an accepted jurisdiction of the
       <a href="/wiki/OECD" title="OECD">
        OECD
       </a>
       and Caribbean
       <a href="/wiki/Financial_Action_Task_Force_on_Money_Laundering" title="Financial Action Task Force on Money Laundering">
        Financial Action Task Force on Money Laundering
       </a>
       . The country enforces Anti-
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Money_Laundering" title="Money Laundering">
        Money Laundering
       </a>
       and
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Counter-Terrorism" title="Counter-Terrorism">
        Counter-Terrorism
       </a>
       funding compliance.
       <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">
        [
        <i>
         <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">
          <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (September 2013)">
           citation needed
          </span>
         </a>
        </i>
        ]
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h4>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Foreign_Account_Tax_Compliance_Act">
        Foreign Account Tax Compliance Act
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Cura%C3%A7ao&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Foreign Account Tax Compliance Act">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h4>
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Historic_Area_of_Willemstad,_Inner_City_and_Harbour,_Cura%C3%A7ao-139160.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1200" data-file-width="1600" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/38/Historic_Area_of_Willemstad%2C_Inner_City_and_Harbour%2C_Cura%C3%A7ao-139160.jpg/220px-Historic_Area_of_Willemstad%2C_Inner_City_and_Harbour%2C_Cura%C3%A7ao-139160.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/38/Historic_Area_of_Willemstad%2C_Inner_City_and_Harbour%2C_Cura%C3%A7ao-139160.jpg/330px-Historic_Area_of_Willemstad%2C_Inner_City_and_Harbour%2C_Cura%C3%A7ao-139160.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/38/Historic_Area_of_Willemstad%2C_Inner_City_and_Harbour%2C_Cura%C3%A7ao-139160.jpg/440px-Historic_Area_of_Willemstad%2C_Inner_City_and_Harbour%2C_Cura%C3%A7ao-139160.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Historic_Area_of_Willemstad,_Inner_City_and_Harbour,_Cura%C3%A7ao-139160.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         Banco di Caribe at Willemstad
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       On June 30, 2014, Curaçao
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-59">
        <a href="#cite_note-59">
         [59]
        </a>
       </sup>
       was deemed to have an Inter-Governmental Agreement (IGA) with the United States of America with respect to the "Foreign Account Tax Compliance Act" of the United States of America.
      </p>
      <p>
       The Model 1 Agreement
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-60">
        <a href="#cite_note-60">
         [60]
        </a>
       </sup>
       recognizes the Kingdom of the Netherlands and states that the agreement relates to Curaçao. This agreement recognizes the following: the Tax Information Exchange Agreement (TIEA) with respect to taxes, which was signed in Washington, D.C. on 17 April 2002 between the Government of the Netherlands Antilles with respect to Curaçao and the Government of the United States of America.
      </p>
      <p>
       The exchange of Notes between the Governments via the respective Ministry of Foreign Affairs "dated 31 October 2014 and 4 November 2014 between the Parties regarding the application of the TIEA in light of the dissolution of the Netherlands Antilles" of which Curaçao was a member country. On 27 March 2017, the U.S. Department of Treasury site disclosed that the agreement and related contracts were "in force" since 3 August 2016.
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Trade">
        Trade
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Cura%C3%A7ao&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Trade">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <p>
       Curaçao trades mainly with the United States, Venezuela, and the European Union. It has an Association Agreement with the European Union which allows companies which do business in and via Curaçao to export products to European markets,
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-61">
        <a href="#cite_note-61">
         [61]
        </a>
       </sup>
       free of import duties and quotas. It is also a participant in the US
       <a href="/wiki/Caribbean_Basin_Initiative" title="Caribbean Basin Initiative">
        Caribbean Basin Initiative
       </a>
       allowing it to have preferential access to the US market.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-62">
        <a href="#cite_note-62">
         [62]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Prostitution">
        Prostitution
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Cura%C3%A7ao&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Prostitution">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       See also:
       <a href="/wiki/Prostitution_in_the_Dutch_Caribbean#Curacao" title="Prostitution in the Dutch Caribbean">
        Prostitution in the Dutch Caribbean § Curacao
       </a>
      </div>
      <p>
       <a href="/wiki/Prostitution" title="Prostitution">
        Prostitution
       </a>
       in Curaçao is legal only for foreign women who get a temporary permit to work in the large open-air brothel called "
       <a href="/wiki/Le_Mirage_(brothel)" title="Le Mirage (brothel)">
        Le Mirage
       </a>
       " or "Campo Alegre" that has operated near the airport since the 1940s, and for the men (locals included) who make use of their services. Curaçao monitors, contains and regulates the industry. The government states that the workers in these establishments are thereby given a safe environment and access to medical practitioners. This approach does exclude local women (or men) to legally make a living from prostitution and does lead to loss of local income as the foreign prostitutes send or take most of their earnings home.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-63">
        <a href="#cite_note-63">
         [63]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       The
       <a href="/wiki/United_States_Department_of_State" title="United States Department of State">
        U.S. State Department
       </a>
       has cited anecdotal evidence claiming that, "Curaçao...[is a] destination island... for women trafficked for the sex trade from Peru, Brazil, Colombia, the Dominican Republic, and Haiti, according to local observers. At least 500 foreign women reportedly are in prostitution throughout the five islands of the Antilles, some of whom have been trafficked."
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-trafficking192_64-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-trafficking192-64">
         [64]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The US Department of State has said that the government of Curaçao frequently underestimates the extent of
       <a href="/wiki/Human_trafficking" title="Human trafficking">
        human trafficking
       </a>
       problems.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-trafficking192_64-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-trafficking192-64">
         [64]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>

        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">

      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Languages">
        Languages
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Cura%C3%A7ao&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Languages">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <p>
       Curaçao is a
       <a href="/wiki/Multilingualism" title="Multilingualism">
        polyglot
       </a>
       society. The official languages are
       <a href="/wiki/Dutch_language" title="Dutch language">
        Dutch
       </a>
       ,
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Papiamentu" title="Papiamentu">
        Papiamentu
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/English_language" title="English language">
        English
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-official-languages_1-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-official-languages-1">
         [1]
        </a>
       </sup>
       However, Dutch is the sole language for all administration and legal matters.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-67">
        <a href="#cite_note-67">
         [67]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Most of Curaçao's population is able to converse in at least two of the languages of Papiamentu, Dutch, English, and
       <a href="/wiki/Spanish_language" title="Spanish language">
        Spanish
       </a>
       .
      </p>
      <p>
       The most widely spoken language is Papiamentu, an African creole with Portuguese, Dutch and Spanish influences, spoken in all levels of society. Papiamentu was introduced as a language of
       <a href="/wiki/Primary_school" title="Primary school">
        primary school
       </a>
       education in 1993, making Curaçao one of a handful of places where a creole language is used as a medium to acquire basic literacy.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Liddicoat2007_68-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-Liddicoat2007-68">
         [68]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Spanish and English also have a long historical presence in Curaçao. Spanish became an important language in the 18th century due to the close economic ties with Spanish colonies in what are now Venezuela and Colombia
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Putte_15-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-Putte-15">
         [15]
        </a>
       </sup>
       and several
       <a href="/wiki/Venezuela" title="Venezuela">
        Venezuelan
       </a>
       TV networks are received. Use of English dates to the early 19th century, when the British took Curaçao and
       <a href="/wiki/Bonaire" title="Bonaire">
        Bonaire
       </a>
       . When Dutch rule resumed in 1815, officials already noted wide use of the language.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Putte_15-2">
        <a href="#cite_note-Putte-15">
         [15]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       According to the 2001 census, Papiamentu is the
       <a href="/wiki/First_language" title="First language">
        first language
       </a>
       of 81.2% of the population. Dutch is the first language of 8%, Spanish of 4%, and English of 2.9%.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-cbs_69-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-cbs-69">
         [69]
        </a>
       </sup>
       However, these numbers divide the population in terms of first language and do not account for the high rate of
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bilingualism" title="Bilingualism">
        bilingualism
       </a>
       in the population of Curaçao.
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Ethnicities">
        Ethnicities
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Cura%C3%A7ao&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Ethnicities">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Bulawaya-1.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1780" data-file-width="2014" height="194" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b2/Bulawaya-1.jpg/220px-Bulawaya-1.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b2/Bulawaya-1.jpg/330px-Bulawaya-1.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b2/Bulawaya-1.jpg/440px-Bulawaya-1.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Bulawaya-1.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         A Bulawaya dance
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       Because of its history, the island's population comes from a number of ethnic backgrounds. While the majority of Curaçaoans are of
       <a href="/wiki/Afro-Cura%C3%A7aoan" title="Afro-Curaçaoan">
        Black African descent
       </a>
       , there are sizeable minorities of
       <a href="/wiki/Dutch_people" title="Dutch people">
        Dutch
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Latin_Americans" title="Latin Americans">
        Latin American
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/French_people" title="French people">
        French
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/South_Asia" title="South Asia">
        South Asian
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/East_Asia" title="East Asia">
        East Asian
       </a>
       (including
       <a href="/wiki/Javanese_people" title="Javanese people">
        Javanese
       </a>
       who descend largely from workers contracted from the island of
       <a href="/wiki/Java" title="Java">
        Java
       </a>
       in the former
       <a href="/wiki/Dutch_East_Indies" title="Dutch East Indies">
        Dutch East Indies
       </a>
       (modern
       <a href="/wiki/Indonesia" title="Indonesia">
        Indonesia
       </a>
       )),
       <a href="/wiki/Portuguese_people" title="Portuguese people">
        Portuguese
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Levant" title="Levant">
        Levantine
       </a>
       people. Additionally, there are both
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sephardic" title="Sephardic">
        Sephardic
       </a>
       and
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ashkenazi" title="Ashkenazi">
        Ashkenazi
       </a>
       Jews.
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Religion">
        Religion
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Cura%C3%A7ao&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: Religion">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="thumb tright" style="">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:200px">
        <div style="background-color:white;margin:auto;position:relative;width:200px;height:200px;overflow:hidden;border-radius:100px;border:1px solid black">

         </div>
