         </div>
         <div class="transborder" style="position:absolute;width:100px;line-height:0;left:100px; top:100px; border-width:100px 0 0 128.91922317851px; border-left-color:SkyBlue">
         </div>
         <div style="position:absolute;line-height:0;border-style:solid;left:0;top:0;border-width:0 200px 100px 0;border-color:SkyBlue">
         </div>
         <div style="position:absolute;line-height:0;border-style:solid;left:0;top:0;border-width:0 100px 200px 0;border-color:SkyBlue">
         </div>
         <div class="transborder" style="position:absolute;width:100px;line-height:0;right:100px; top:100px; border-width:99.046142569665px 13.779029068464px 0 0; border-top-color:DodgerBlue">
         </div>
         <div style="position:absolute;line-height:0;border-style:solid;left:0;top:0;border-width:0 200px 100px 0;border-color:DodgerBlue">
         </div>
        </div>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <dl>
          <dt>
           Religion in Curaçao
           <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-CIACuraçao_70-0">
            <a href="#cite_note-CIACuraçao-70">
             [70]
            </a>
           </sup>
          </dt>
         </dl>
         <div class="legend" style="-webkit-column-break-inside: avoid;page-break-inside: avoid;break-inside: avoid-column">
          <span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color:DodgerBlue; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;">
          </span>
          Roman Catholic (72.8%)
         </div>
         <div class="legend" style="-webkit-column-break-inside: avoid;page-break-inside: avoid;break-inside: avoid-column">
          <span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color:SkyBlue; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;">
          </span>
          Protestant (16.7%)
         </div>
         <div class="legend" style="-webkit-column-break-inside: avoid;page-break-inside: avoid;break-inside: avoid-column">
          <span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color:Black; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;">
          </span>
          None (6%)
         </div>
         <div class="legend" style="-webkit-column-break-inside: avoid;page-break-inside: avoid;break-inside: avoid-column">
          <span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color:grey; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;">
          </span>
          Other (Jewish, Hindu, Muslim, etc.) (3.8%)
         </div>
         <div class="legend" style="-webkit-column-break-inside: avoid;page-break-inside: avoid;break-inside: avoid-column">
          <span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color:LightGrey; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;">
          </span>
          Unspecified (0.6%)
         </div>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       The religious breakdown of the population of Curaçao, according to a 2011 estimate:
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-CIACuraçao_70-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-CIACuraçao-70">
         [70]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <ul>
       <li>
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Roman_Catholic" title="Roman Catholic">
         Roman Catholic
        </a>
        ;
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-CIACuraçao_70-2">
         <a href="#cite_note-CIACuraçao-70">
          [70]
         </a>
        </sup>
        72.8%
       </li>
       <li>
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Pentecostal" title="Pentecostal">
         Pentecostal
        </a>
        ;
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-CIACuraçao_70-3">
         <a href="#cite_note-CIACuraçao-70">
          [70]
         </a>
        </sup>
        6.6%
       </li>
       <li>
        other
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Protestant" title="Protestant">
         Protestant
        </a>
        ;
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-CIACuraçao_70-4">
         <a href="#cite_note-CIACuraçao-70">
          [70]
         </a>
        </sup>
        3.2%
       </li>
       <li>
        <a href="/wiki/Adventism" title="Adventism">
         Adventist
        </a>
        ;
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-CIACuraçao_70-5">
         <a href="#cite_note-CIACuraçao-70">
          [70]
         </a>
        </sup>
        3%
       </li>
       <li>
        <a href="/wiki/Jehovah%27s_Witnesses" title="Jehovah's Witnesses">
         Jehovah's Witnesses
        </a>
        ;
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-CIACuraçao_70-6">
         <a href="#cite_note-CIACuraçao-70">
          [70]
         </a>
        </sup>
        2%
       </li>
       <li>
        <a href="/wiki/Evangelicalism" title="Evangelicalism">
         Evangelical
        </a>
        ;
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-CIACuraçao_70-7">
         <a href="#cite_note-CIACuraçao-70">
          [70]
         </a>
        </sup>
        1.9%
       </li>
       <li>
        Other;
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-CIACuraçao_70-8">
         <a href="#cite_note-CIACuraçao-70">
          [70]
         </a>
        </sup>
        3.8%
       </li>
       <li>
        None;
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-CIACuraçao_70-9">
         <a href="#cite_note-CIACuraçao-70">
          [70]
         </a>
        </sup>
        6%
       </li>
       <li>
        Unspecified;
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-CIACuraçao_70-10">
         <a href="#cite_note-CIACuraçao-70">
          [70]
         </a>
        </sup>
        0.6%
       </li>
      </ul>
      <p>
       This includes a shift towards the charismatic renewal or charismatic movement since the mid-1970s. Other denominations include the
       <a href="/wiki/Seventh-day_Adventist_Church" title="Seventh-day Adventist Church">
        Seventh-day Adventist Church
       </a>
       and the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Methodist_Church" title="Methodist Church">
        Methodist Church
       </a>
       . Alongside these Christian denominations, some inhabitants practice
       <a href="/wiki/Montamentu" title="Montamentu">
        Montamentu
       </a>
       and other diaspora African religions.
       <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">
        [
        <i>
         <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">
          <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (September 2015)">
           citation needed
          </span>
         </a>
        </i>
        ]
       </sup>
       Like elsewhere in Latin America, Pentecostalism is on the rise. There are also practising Muslims and Hindus.
      </p>
      <p>
       The Catholic diocese of
       <a href="/wiki/Roman_Catholic_Diocese_of_Willemstad" title="Roman Catholic Diocese of Willemstad">
        Willemstad
       </a>
       encompasses all the territory of the
       <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_the_Netherlands" title="Kingdom of the Netherlands">
        Kingdom of the Netherlands
       </a>
       in the
       <a href="/wiki/Caribbean" title="Caribbean">
        Caribbean
       </a>
       which includes
       <a href="/wiki/Aruba" title="Aruba">
        Aruba
       </a>
       , Curaçao,
       <a href="/wiki/Sint_Maarten" title="Sint Maarten">
        Sint Maarten
       </a>
       , and the islands of
       <a href="/wiki/Bonaire" title="Bonaire">
        Bonaire
       </a>
       ,
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/St._Eustatius" title="St. Eustatius">
        St. Eustatius
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Saba" title="Saba">
        Saba
       </a>
       . The diocese is also a member of the
       <a href="/wiki/Antilles_Episcopal_Conference" title="Antilles Episcopal Conference">
        Antilles Episcopal Conference
       </a>
       .
      </p>
      <p>
       While small, Curaçao's
       <a href="/wiki/Judaism" title="Judaism">
        Jewish
       </a>
       community has had a significant impact on the island's history.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-history_12-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-history-12">
         [12]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Curaçao has the oldest active Jewish congregation in the
       <a href="/wiki/Americas" title="Americas">
        Americas
       </a>
       , dating to 1651. The
       <a href="/wiki/Cura%C3%A7ao_synagogue" title="Curaçao synagogue">
        Curaçao synagogue
       </a>
       is the oldest
       <a href="/wiki/Synagogue" title="Synagogue">
        synagogue
       </a>
       of the Americas in continuous use, since its completion in 1732 on the site of a previous synagogue.
      </p>
      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Education">
        Education
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Cura%C3%A7ao&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: Education">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>
      <p>
       Public education is based on the Dutch educational system and besides the public schools, private and parochial schools are also available. Since the introduction of a new public education law in 1992, compulsory primary education starts at age six and continues six years, secondary lasts for another five.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-edu_71-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-edu-71">
         [71]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       The main institute of higher learning is the
       <a href="/wiki/University_of_Cura%C3%A7ao" title="University of Curaçao">
        University of Curaçao
       </a>
       , enrolling 2,100 students.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-edu_71-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-edu-71">
         [71]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The comprehensive model of education is under influences from both Dutch and American's education offering. Other higher education offering on the island include
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Offshore_Medical_School_in_the_Caribbean" title="Offshore Medical School in the Caribbean">
        offshore medical schools
       </a>
       , language schools and academies for fine art, music, police, teacher and nurse-training.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-72">
        <a href="#cite_note-72">
         [72]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Culture">
        Culture
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Cura%C3%A7ao&amp;action=edit&amp;section=28" title="Edit section: Culture">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Literature">
        Literature
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Cura%C3%A7ao&amp;action=edit&amp;section=29" title="Edit section: Literature">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <p>
       Despite the island's relatively small population, the diversity of languages and cultural influences on Curaçao have generated a remarkable literary tradition, primarily in
       <a href="/wiki/Dutch_language" title="Dutch language">
        Dutch
       </a>
       and
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Papiamentu" title="Papiamentu">
        Papiamentu
       </a>
       . The oral traditions of the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Arawak_peoples" title="Arawak peoples">
        Arawak
       </a>
       <a href="/wiki/Indigenous_peoples" title="Indigenous peoples">
        indigenous peoples
       </a>
       are lost. West African slaves brought the tales of
       <a href="/wiki/Anansi" title="Anansi">
        Anansi
       </a>
       , thus forming the basis of Papiamentu literature. The first published work in Papiamentu was a poem by
       <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Joseph_Sickman_Corsen&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Joseph Sickman Corsen (page does not exist)">
        Joseph Sickman Corsen
       </a>
       entitled
       <i>
        Atardi
       </i>
       , published in the
       <i>
        La Cruz
       </i>
       newspaper in 1905. Throughout Curaçaoan literature,
       <a href="/wiki/Narrative" title="Narrative">
        narrative
       </a>
       techniques and metaphors best characterized as
       <a href="/wiki/Magic_realism" title="Magic realism">
        magic realism
       </a>
       tend to predominate. Novelists and poets from Curaçao have made an impressive contribution to
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Caribbean_Literature" title="Caribbean Literature">
        Caribbean
       </a>
       and
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Dutch_literature" title="Dutch literature">
        Dutch literature
       </a>
       . Best known are
       <a href="/wiki/Cola_Debrot" title="Cola Debrot">
        Cola Debrot
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Frank_Martinus_Arion" title="Frank Martinus Arion">
        Frank Martinus Arion
       </a>
       , Pierre Lauffer, Elis Juliana, Guillermo Rosario, Boeli van Leeuwen and
       <a href="/wiki/Tip_Marugg" title="Tip Marugg">
        Tip Marugg
       </a>
       .
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Cuisine">
        Cuisine
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Cura%C3%A7ao&amp;action=edit&amp;section=30" title="Edit section: Cuisine">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <p>
       Local food is called
       <i>
        Krioyo
       </i>
       (pronounced the same as
       <i>
        criollo
       </i>
       , the Spanish word for "Creole") and boasts a blend of flavours and techniques best compared to Caribbean cuisine and Latin American cuisine. Dishes common in Curaçao are found in
       <a href="/wiki/Aruba" title="Aruba">
        Aruba
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Bonaire" title="Bonaire">
        Bonaire
       </a>
       as well. Popular dishes include: stobá (a stew made with various ingredients such as
       <a href="/wiki/Papaya" title="Papaya">
        papaya
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Beef" title="Beef">
        beef
       </a>
       or
       <a href="/wiki/Goat" title="Goat">
        goat
       </a>
       ), Guiambo (soup made from
       <a href="/wiki/Okra" title="Okra">
        okra
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Seafood" title="Seafood">
        seafood
       </a>
       ), kadushi (cactus soup), sopi mondongo (intestine soup), funchi (cornmeal paste similar to
       <a href="/wiki/Fufu" title="Fufu">
        fufu
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Ugali" title="Ugali">
        ugali
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Polenta" title="Polenta">
        polenta
       </a>
       ) and a lot of fish and other seafood. The ubiquitous side dish is fried
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Plantain_(cooking)" title="Plantain (cooking)">
        plantain
       </a>
       . Local bread rolls are made according to a
       <a href="/wiki/Portugal" title="Portugal">
        Portuguese
       </a>
       recipe. All around the island, there are snèks which serve local dishes as well as alcoholic drinks in a manner akin to the English
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Public_house" title="Public house">
        public house
       </a>
       .
      </p>
      <p>
       The ubiquitous breakfast dish is pastechi: fried pastry with fillings of cheese, tuna, ham, or ground meat. Around the holiday season special dishes are consumed, such as the
       <a href="/wiki/Hallaca" title="Hallaca">
        hallaca
       </a>
       and pekelé, made out of
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Salt_cod" title="Salt cod">
        salt cod
       </a>
       . At weddings and other special occasions a variety of kos dushi are served: kokada (coconut sweets), ko'i lechi (condensed milk and sugar sweet) and tentalaria (peanut sweets). The
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Cura%C3%A7ao_liqueur" title="Curaçao liqueur">
        Curaçao liqueur
       </a>
       was developed here, when a local experimented with the rinds of the local
       <a href="/wiki/Citrus" title="Citrus">
        citrus
       </a>
       fruit known as
       <a href="/wiki/Laraha" title="Laraha">
        laraha
       </a>
       .
       <a href="/wiki/Suriname" title="Suriname">
        Surinamese
       </a>
       , Chinese,
       <a href="/wiki/Indonesia" title="Indonesia">
        Indonesian
       </a>
       , Indian and Dutch culinary influences also abound. The island also has a number of Chinese restaurants that serve mainly Indonesian dishes such as
       <a href="/wiki/Satay" title="Satay">
        satay
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Nasi_goreng" title="Nasi goreng">
        nasi goreng
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Lumpia" title="Lumpia">
        lumpia
       </a>
       (which are all Indonesian names for the dishes). Dutch specialties such as
       <a href="/wiki/Croquette" title="Croquette">
        croquettes
       </a>
       and
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Oliebollen" title="Oliebollen">
        oliebollen
       </a>
       are widely served in homes and restaurants.
      </p>
      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Sports">
        Sports
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Cura%C3%A7ao&amp;action=edit&amp;section=31" title="Edit section: Sports">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Jurickson_Profar_(9260642222).jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2139" data-file-width="1507" height="312" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/28/Jurickson_Profar_%289260642222%29.jpg/220px-Jurickson_Profar_%289260642222%29.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/28/Jurickson_Profar_%289260642222%29.jpg/330px-Jurickson_Profar_%289260642222%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/28/Jurickson_Profar_%289260642222%29.jpg/440px-Jurickson_Profar_%289260642222%29.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Jurickson_Profar_(9260642222).jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         <a href="/wiki/Jurickson_Profar" title="Jurickson Profar">
          Jurickson Profar
         </a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       In 2004, the
       <a href="/wiki/Little_League_Baseball" title="Little League Baseball">
        Little League Baseball
       </a>
       team from Willemstad, Curaçao, won the world title in a game against the
       <a href="/wiki/United_States" title="United States">
        United States
       </a>
       champion from
       <a href="/wiki/Thousand_Oaks,_California" title="Thousand Oaks, California">
        Thousand Oaks, California
       </a>
       . The Willemstad lineup included
       <a href="/wiki/Jurickson_Profar" title="Jurickson Profar">
        Jurickson Profar
       </a>
       , the standout shortstop prospect who now plays for the
       <a href="/wiki/Texas_Rangers_(baseball)" title="Texas Rangers (baseball)">
        Texas Rangers
       </a>
       of
       <a href="/wiki/Major_League_Baseball" title="Major League Baseball">
        Major League Baseball
       </a>
       .
      </p>
      <p>
       In the
       <a href="/wiki/2006_World_Baseball_Classic" title="2006 World Baseball Classic">
        2006 World Baseball Classic
       </a>
       , Curaçaoans played for the Netherlands team.
       <a href="/wiki/Shairon_Martis" title="Shairon Martis">
        Shairon Martis
       </a>
       , born in
       <a href="/wiki/Willemstad" title="Willemstad">
        Willemstad
       </a>
       , contributed to the Dutch team by throwing a seven-inning no-hitter against Panama (the game was stopped due to the
       <a href="/wiki/Mercy_rule" title="Mercy rule">
        mercy rule
       </a>
       ).
      </p>
      <p>
       The 2010 documentary film,
       <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Boys_of_Summer_(film)&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Boys of Summer (film) (page does not exist)">
        Boys of Summer
       </a>
       ,
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-73">
        <a href="#cite_note-73">
         [73]
        </a>
       </sup>
       details Curaçao's Pabao Little League All-Stars winning their country's eighth straight championship at the 2008 Little League World Series, then going on to defeat other teams, including Puerto Rico and the Dominican Republic, and earning a spot in Williamsport.
      </p>
      <p>
       The prevailing trade winds and warm water make Curaçao a location for windsurfing.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-74">
        <a href="#cite_note-74">
         [74]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-75">
        <a href="#cite_note-75">
         [75]
        </a>
       </sup>
       One factor is that the deep water around Curaçao makes it difficult to lay marks for major windsurfing events, thus hindering the island's success as a windsurfing destination.
      </p>
      <p>
       There is warm, clear water around the island. Scuba divers and snorkelers may have visibility up to 30 metres (98 feet) at the Curaçao Underwater Marine Park, which stretches along 20 kilometres (12 miles) of Curaçao's southern coastline.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-76">
        <a href="#cite_note-76">
         [76]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       Curaçao participated in the
       <a href="/wiki/2013_CARIFTA_Games" title="2013 CARIFTA Games">
        2013 CARIFTA Games
       </a>
       . Kevin Philbert stood third in the under-20 male Long Jump with a distance of 7.36 metres (24.15 feet). Vanessa Philbert stood second the under-17 female 1,500 metres (4,900 feet) with a time of 4:47.97.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-cfpi_1_77-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-cfpi_1-77">
         [77]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-milesplit_1_78-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-milesplit_1-78">
         [78]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-cfpi_2_79-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-cfpi_2-79">
         [79]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-milesplit_2_80-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-milesplit_2-80">
         [80]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Infrastructure">
        Infrastructure
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Cura%C3%A7ao&amp;action=edit&amp;section=32" title="Edit section: Infrastructure">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Airport">
        Airport
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Cura%C3%A7ao&amp;action=edit&amp;section=33" title="Edit section: Airport">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <p>
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hato_International_Airport" title="Hato International Airport">
        Hato International Airport
       </a>
       is located on the island. Its main runway parallels, and is adjacent to, the northern coast.
      </p>
      <p>
       It has services to the Caribbean region, South America, North America and Europe. Hato Airport is a fairly large facility, with the third longest commercial runway in the Caribbean region after Rafael Hernández Airport in Puerto Rico and Pointe-à-Pitre International Airport in Guadeloupe. The airport serves as a main base for
       <a href="/wiki/Insel_Air" title="Insel Air">
        Insel Air
       </a>
       , the national airline of Curaçao.
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Bridges">
        Bridges
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Cura%C3%A7ao&amp;action=edit&amp;section=34" title="Edit section: Bridges">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Curacao-Bridges-2013.JPG">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3130" data-file-width="4608" height="149" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/50/Curacao-Bridges-2013.JPG/220px-Curacao-Bridges-2013.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/50/Curacao-Bridges-2013.JPG/330px-Curacao-Bridges-2013.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/50/Curacao-Bridges-2013.JPG/440px-Curacao-Bridges-2013.JPG 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Curacao-Bridges-2013.JPG" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         The
         <a href="/wiki/Queen_Emma_Bridge" title="Queen Emma Bridge">
          Queen Emma
         </a>
         (semi-open), and the
         <a href="/wiki/Queen_Juliana_Bridge" title="Queen Juliana Bridge">
          Queen Juliana
         </a>
         .
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       The
       <a href="/wiki/Queen_Emma_Bridge" title="Queen Emma Bridge">
        Queen Emma Bridge
       </a>
       , a 168 metres (551 ft) long
       <a href="/wiki/Pontoon_bridge" title="Pontoon bridge">
        pontoon bridge
       </a>
       , connects pedestrians between the Punda and Otrobanda districts.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-81">
        <a href="#cite_note-81">
         [81]
        </a>
       </sup>
       This swings open to allow the passage of ships to and from the port.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-queen_82-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-queen-82">
         [82]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The bridge was originally opened in 1888 and the current bridge was installed in 1939.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-emmabridge_83-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-emmabridge-83">
         [83]
        </a>
       </sup>
       It is best known and, more often than not, referred to by the locals as "Our Swinging Old Lady".
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-84">
        <a href="#cite_note-84">
         [84]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       The
       <a href="/wiki/Queen_Juliana_Bridge" title="Queen Juliana Bridge">
        Queen Juliana Bridge
       </a>
       connects mobile traffic between the same two districts. At 185 feet (56 m) above the sea, it is one of the highest bridges in the Caribbean.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-queen_82-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-queen-82">
         [82]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Utilities">
        Utilities
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Cura%C3%A7ao&amp;action=edit&amp;section=35" title="Edit section: Utilities">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <p>
       A private company, and full member of
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Caribbean_Electric_Utility_Services_Corporation_(CARILEC)" title="Caribbean Electric Utility Services Corporation (CARILEC)">
        CARILEC
       </a>
       , Aqualectra, delivers potable water and electricity to the island. Rates are controlled by the government. Water is produced by
       <a href="/wiki/Reverse_osmosis" title="Reverse osmosis">
        reverse osmosis
       </a>
       or
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Desalinization" title="Desalinization">
        desalinization
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-aqualectra.com_85-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-aqualectra.com-85">
         [85]
        </a>
       </sup>
       It services 69,000 households and companies using 130,000 water and electric meters.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-aqualectra.com_85-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-aqualectra.com-85">
         [85]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>

                   <tr>
                    <td class="navbox-abovebelow" colspan="2">
                     <div>
                      <ul>
                       <li>
                        <sup>
                         <small>
                          3
                         </small>
                        </sup>
                        <span class="wrap">
                         Became
                         <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_the_Netherlands#Countries" title="Kingdom of the Netherlands">
                          constituent countries
                         </a>
                         of the Kingdom of the Netherlands;
                         <a href="/wiki/Suriname_(Kingdom_of_the_Netherlands)" title="Suriname (Kingdom of the Netherlands)">
                          Suriname
                         </a>
                         gained
                         <a href="/wiki/Suriname" title="Suriname">
                          full independence
                         </a>
                         in 1975, Curaçao and Dependencies was renamed to the
                         <a href="/wiki/Netherlands_Antilles" title="Netherlands Antilles">
                          Netherlands Antilles
                         </a>
                         , which was eventually dissolved in 2010.
                        </span>
                       </li>
                      </ul>
                     </div>
